     114                 :            : /*
     115                 :            :  * The "vtlinks" array keeps information about each recently-updated tuple
     116                 :            :  * ("recent" meaning its XMAX is too new to let us recycle the tuple).
     117                 :            :  * We store the tuple's own TID as well as its t_ctid (its link to the next
     118                 :            :  * newer tuple version).  Searching in this array allows us to follow update
     119                 :            :  * chains backwards from newer to older tuples.  When we move a member of an
     120                 :            :  * update chain, we must move *all* the live members of the chain, so that we
     121                 :            :  * can maintain their t_ctid link relationships (we must not just overwrite
     122                 :            :  * t_ctid in an existing tuple).
     123                 :            :  *
     124                 :            :  * Note: because t_ctid links can be stale (this would only occur if a prior
     125                 :            :  * VACUUM crashed partway through), it is possible that new_tid points to an
     126                 :            :  * empty slot or unrelated tuple.  We have to check the linkage as we follow
     127                 :            :  * it, just as is done in EvalPlanQual.
     128                 :            :  */

     890                 :            :  *
     891                 :            :  * The function is called by vacuumStatement once for each relation to vacuum.
     892                 :            :  * In order to connect QD and QE work for vacuum, we employ a little
     893                 :            :  * complicated mechanism here; we separate one relation vacuum process
     894                 :            :  * to a separate steps, depending on the type of storage (heap/AO),
     895                 :            :  * and perform each step in separate transactions, so that QD can open
     896                 :            :  * a distributed transaction and embrace QE work inside it.  As opposed to
     897                 :            :  * old postgres code, where one transaction is opened and closed for each
     898                 :            :  * auxiliary relation, here a transaction processes them as a set starting
     899                 :            :  * from the base relation.  This is the entry point of one base relation,
     900                 :            :  * and QD makes some decision what kind of stage we perform, and tells it
     901                 :            :  * to QE with vacstmt fields through dispatch.
     902                 :            :  *
     903                 :            :  * For heap VACUUM FULL, we need two transactions.  One is to move tuples
     904                 :            :  * from a page to another, to empty out last pages, which typically goes
     905                 :            :  * into repair_frag.  We used to perform truncate operation there, but
     906                 :            :  * it required to record transaction commit locally, which is not pleasant
     907                 :            :  * if QD decides to cancel the whoe distributed transaction.  So the truncate
     908                 :            :  * step is separated to a second transaction.  This two step operation is
     909                 :            :  * performed on both base relation and toast relation at the same time.
     910                 :            :  *
     911                 :            :  * Lazy vacuum to heap is one step operation.
     912                 :            :  *
     913                 :            :  * AO compaction is rather complicated.  There are four phases.
     914                 :            :  *   - prepare phase
     915                 :            :  *   - compaction phase
     916                 :            :  *   - drop phase
     917                 :            :  *   - cleanup phase
     918                 :            :  * Out of these, compaction and drop phase might repeat multiple times.
     919                 :            :  * We go through the list of available segment files by looking up catalog,
     920                 :            :  * and perform a compaction operation, which appends the whole segfile
     921                 :            :  * to another available one, if the source segfile looks to be dirty enough.
     922                 :            :  * If we find such one and perform compaction, the next step is drop. In
     923                 :            :  * order to allow concurrent read it is required for the drop phase to
     924                 :            :  * be a separate transaction.  We mark the segfile as an awaiting-drop
     925                 :            :  * in the catalog, and the drop phase actually drops the segfile from the
     926                 :            :  * disk.  There are some cases where we cannot drop the segfile immediately,
     927                 :            :  * in which case we just skip it and leave the catalog to have awaiting-drop
     928                 :            :  * state for this segfile.  Aside from the compaction and drop phases, the
     929                 :            :  * rest is much simpler.  The prepare phase is to truncate unnecessary
     930                 :            :  * blocks after the logical EOF, and the cleanup phase does normal heap
     931                 :            :  * vacuum on auxiliary relations (toast, aoseg, block directory, visimap,)
     932                 :            :  * as well as updating stats info in catalog.  Keep in mind that if the
     933                 :            :  * vacuum is full, we need the same two steps as the heap base relation
     934                 :            :  * case.  So cleanup phase in AO may consume two transactions.
     935                 :            :  *
     936                 :            :  * While executing these multiple transactions, we acquire a session
     937                 :            :  * lock across transactions, in order to keep concurrent work on the
     938                 :            :  * same relation away.  It doesn't look intuitive, though, if you look
     939                 :            :  * at QE work, because from its perspective it is always one step, therefore
     940                 :            :  * there is no session lock technically (we actually acquire and release
     941                 :            :  * it as it's harmless.)  Session lock doesn't work here, because QE
     942                 :            :  * is under a distributed transaction and we haven't supported session
     943                 :            :  * lock recording in transaction prepare.  This should be ok as far as
     944                 :            :  * we are dealing with user table, because other MPP work also tries
     945                 :            :  * to take a relation lock, which would conflict with this vacuum work
     946                 :            :  * on master.  Be careful with catalog tables, because we take locks on
     947                 :            :  * them and release soon much before the end of transaction.  That means
     948                 :            :  * QE still needs to deal with concurrent work well.
     949                 :            :  */
     950                 :            : static void

     953                 :            :                                                  bool for_wraparound, bool isTopLevel)

    1715                 :            : /*
    1716                 :            :  *      vac_update_relstats() -- update statistics for one relation
    1717                 :            :  *
    1718                 :            :  *              Update the whole-relation statistics that are kept in its pg_class
    1719                 :            :  *              row.  There are additional stats that will be updated if we are
    1720                 :            :  *              doing ANALYZE, but we always update these stats.  This routine works
    1721                 :            :  *              for both index and heap relation entries in pg_class.
    1722                 :            :  *
    1723                 :            :  *              We violate transaction semantics here by overwriting the rel's
    1724                 :            :  *              existing pg_class tuple with the new values.  This is reasonably
    1725                 :            :  *              safe since the new values are correct whether or not this transaction
    1726                 :            :  *              commits.  The reason for this is that if we updated these tuples in
    1727                 :            :  *              the usual way, vacuuming pg_class itself wouldn't work very well ---
    1728                 :            :  *              by the time we got done with a vacuum cycle, most of the tuples in
    1729                 :            :  *              pg_class would've been obsoleted.  Of course, this only works for
    1730                 :            :  *              fixed-size never-null columns, but these are.
    1731                 :            :  *
    1732                 :            :  *              This routine is shared by full VACUUM, lazy VACUUM, and stand-alone
    1733                 :            :  *              ANALYZE.
    1734                 :            :  */

    2416                 :            : /*
    2417                 :            :  * vacuum_heap_rel()
    2418                 :            :  *
    2419                 :            :  * This is the workhorse of full_vacuum_rel for heap tables.  This is called
    2420                 :            :  * twice per relation per command.  In the first call, we scan the relation
    2421                 :            :  * first to identify dead tuples and find free spaces, then clean up indexes

    2570                 :            : 
    2571                 :            : /*
    2572                 :            :  *      full_vacuum_rel() -- perform FULL VACUUM for one heap relation
    2573                 :            :  *
    2574                 :            :  *              This routine vacuums a single heap, cleans out its indexes, and
    2575                 :            :  *              updates its num_pages and num_tuples statistics.
    2576                 :            :  *
    2577                 :            :  *              At entry, we have already established a transaction and opened
    2578                 :            :  *              and locked the relation.
    2579                 :            :  *
    2580                 :            :  *              The return value indicates whether this function has held off
    2581                 :            :  *              interrupts -- caller must RESUME_INTERRUPTS() after commit if true.
